## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population growth ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is the time-derivative of population size P, which is the standard setup for continuous-time population dynamics in ecology. Typical relationships express growth as density-independent terms (∝ P) plus density-dependent regulation (functions of P) and sometimes explicit time forcing (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resources, constant per-capita rate)
- Linear time-varying growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (changing environment causing trend in per-capita growth)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (crowding reduces growth when c1 < 0)
- Logistic differential equation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P) (carrying-capacity regulation in ODE form; equivalent to rP(1-P/K) up to reparameterization)
- Theta-logistic (generalized logistic): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P**c2) (flexible curvature of density dependence)
- Gompertz growth (ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (density dependence acts on log-scale; asymmetric approach to capacity)
- Richards / generalized logistic (ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P**c2) * P**c3 (adds extra shape flexibility via additional P exponent)
- Strong crowding / higher-order regulation: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**c2 (c2 > 1 captures nonlinear competition/self-limitation)
- Allee effect (weak/strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) (positive density dependence at low P plus upper regulation)
- Harvesting/removal (constant effort): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P) - c2 (constant offtake; can drive extinction)
- Proportional harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P) - c2 * P (per-capita mortality/harvest in addition to regulation)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment affects per-capita growth)
- Seasonally forced carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) - P) (time-varying effective capacity)
- Phenomenological non-autonomous polynomial: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * t * P + c2 * P**2 (combined time trend and density dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita rate constant → dP_dt proportional to P (straight-line on log(P) vs t)
- Crowding/competition → negative curvature in dP_dt vs P, often a negative P**2 (or higher power) term
- Finite carrying capacity → factor of (c - P) multiplying P; yields stable equilibrium near P ≈ c
- Nonlinear regulation strength → exponent on P inside the limiting term (e.g., P**c) changes how sharply growth slows near capacity
- Asymmetric approach to capacity → log(c/P) factor (Gompertz-type), where regulation intensifies multiplicatively with log-size
- Depensation/Allee threshold → factor (P - c) causing negative growth below a critical population size
- External removals/harvesting → subtractive terms (−c, −c*P) shifting equilibria and enabling extinction thresholds
- Seasonality or cyclic environment → sin(c*t + phase) modulation of coefficients, producing periodic growth accelerations/slowdowns
- Directional environmental change → coefficients depending on t (e.g., c0 + c1*t) producing accelerating/declining growth regimes
- Multiple mechanisms simultaneously → additive combination of density-independent and density-dependent components (e.g., P term plus P**2 term plus t*P term)

GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - exp(-c7*P))*P
Candidate formulas: 50

Let \(P\) be the only effective variable in the GT (note \(t\) does not appear in GT). Rewrite the GT as a fixed function of \(P\):

\[
\text{GT}(P)=a\Big(-1+\frac{P}{b}\Big)\Big(1-\frac{P}{d}\Big)P \;+\; a\big(1-e^{-kP}\big)P
\]
with fixed numbers \(a=0.8450821034\), \(b=5.1153864545\), \(d=34.4388624238\), \(k=0.0968726647352\).

Expand the polynomial part:
\[
a\Big(-1+\frac{P}{b}\Big)\Big(1-\frac{P}{d}\Big)P
= a\left(-P + \Big(\frac1b+\frac1d\Big)P^2 - \frac{1}{bd}P^3\right)
\]
and the exponential part:
\[
a(1-e^{-kP})P = aP - aP e^{-kP}.
\]
So the \(-aP\) and \(+aP\) cancel, giving the simplified exact GT form:
\[
\boxed{\text{GT}(P)= \alpha P^2 + \beta P^3 \;-\; a\,P\,e^{-kP}}
\]
where \(\alpha=a(\frac1b+\frac1d)\neq 0\), \(\beta=-\frac{a}{bd}\neq 0\), and the non-polynomial term is exactly \(-a\,P e^{-kP}\) with fixed \(a,k>0\).

Key consequence: **Any matching candidate must be able to represent a term of the form \(P e^{-kP}\)** (with nonzero coefficient), because this term cannot be produced by pure polynomials, logs, sines, rationals, Max/Abs, or exponentials of \(+kP\) unless the coefficient is forced to 0 (which would not match GT).

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) and determine which candidates can match it.

## GT Analysis

The GT is:
$$f(P) = 0.845(-1 + P/5.115)(1 - P/34.44)P + 0.845(1 - e^{-0.0969P})P$$

Let me expand the first term:
$$(-1 + P/5.115)(1 - P/34.44) = -1 + P/34.44 + P/5.115 - P^2/(5.115 \times 34.44)$$
$$= -1 + P(1/34.44 + 1/5.115) - P^2/176.16$$

Multiplying by $0.845P$:
$$0.845P[-1 + P(0.02904 + 0.19549) - P^2 \cdot 0.005677]$$
$$= 0.845[-P + 0.22453P^2 - 0.005677P^3]$$
$$= -0.004797P^3 + 0.18973P^2 - 0.845P$$

The second term: $0.845(1 - e^{-0.0969P})P = 0.845P - 0.845Pe^{-0.0969P}$

Combining:
$$f(P) = -0.004797P^3 + 0.18973P^2 - 0.845P + 0.845P - 0.845Pe^{-0.0969P}$$
$$= -0.004797P^3 + 0.18973P^2 - 0.845Pe^{-0.0969P}$$

So the GT is: **cubic in P + quadratic in P + P·exp(-aP)** term. The key basis functions are: $P^3$, $P^2$, $P \cdot e^{-aP}$.

Note: There's no dependence on $t$.

Now I need to check which candidates can produce this form. The critical element is the $P \cdot e^{-aP}$ term - this cannot be replicated by polynomials, logarithms, rational functions, sin, Max, or other non-exponential functions.

Let me identify candidates with $\exp(P \cdot \text{const})$ terms:

- **Candidate 20**: $P^3c_0 + P^2c_1 + Pc_2 + Pc_3 + c_4\exp(Pc_5) + c_6$ — Has $c_4\exp(Pc_5)$, but GT needs $P\exp(aP)$, not $\exp(aP)$. [NO MATCH]

- **Candidate 22**: Has $c_7\exp(Pc_8)$ — no $P$ multiplier. [NO MATCH]

- **Candidate 44**: Has $\log(c_6\exp(Pc_7) + 1)$ — this is a softplus, not $Pe^{aP}$. [NO MATCH]

- **Candidate 45**: Same softplus structure. [NO MATCH]

Let me systematically check all candidates. The GT requires a $Pe^{-aP}$ term. No polynomial, rational, log, sin, Max, or abs function can replicate this. Only candidates with explicit $P \cdot \exp(cP)$ or equivalent can match.

None of the candidates have $P \cdot \exp(cP)$ as a term. Candidates 20, 22, 29 have $\exp(cP)$ without the $P$ multiplier. Candidates 44, 45 have $\log(c\exp(cP)+1)$ which is softplus.
